## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: thermo-mechanical constitutive modeling (materials science)
**Analysis**: This task models the stress-strain-temperature relationship of a material. Temperature typically modifies elastic modulus and hardening behavior, while strain determines the mechanical response through linear or nonlinear constitutive laws.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Hooke's law (temperature-dependent): sigma = c0 * epsilon (linear elasticity at fixed T)
- Temperature-dependent modulus: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon (linear elasticity with thermal softening of modulus)
- Quadratic thermal modulus: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T + c2 * T**2) * epsilon (modulus with nonlinear temperature dependence)
- Power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (nonlinear stress-strain in plastic regime)
- Ramberg-Osgood type: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**c2 (elastic-plastic transition)
- Johnson-Cook type (no strain rate): sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (1 + c3 * T) (thermo-mechanical flow stress)
- Johnson-Cook thermal softening: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (1 - c3 * T**c4) (flow stress with thermal softening)
- Exponential thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon * exp(c1 * T) (Arrhenius-like temperature dependence of modulus)
- Polynomial stress-strain: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 + c2 * epsilon**3 (nonlinear elastic or hyperelastic)
- Thermal polynomial with hardening: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon + (c2 + c3 * T) * epsilon**2 (temperature-dependent nonlinear constitutive law)
- Voce-type hardening with temperature: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * (1 - exp(c2 * epsilon)) (saturating hardening with thermal effect)
- Ludwik model with temperature: sigma = c0 * exp(c1 * T) + c2 * epsilon**c3 * exp(c4 * T) (yield stress plus power hardening, both temperature-dependent)
- Thermal expansion offset: sigma = c0 * (epsilon - c1 * T) (stress accounting for thermal strain)
- Combined thermal-strain coupling: sigma = c0 * epsilon * (c1 - T) * (c2 + epsilon**c3) (multiplicative coupling of strain hardening and thermal softening)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Linear proportionality between stress and strain at small strains → multiplicative form c*epsilon, where c depends on temperature
- Thermal softening of elastic modulus → modulus expressed as a decreasing function of T, e.g., (c0 - c1*T) or exp(-c*T)
- Strain hardening saturation → use of (1 - exp(-c*epsilon)) or tanh-like forms to capture diminishing hardening rate
- Power-law strain hardening → epsilon**c with 0 < c < 1 indicates work hardening in metals
- Thermal strain offset → (epsilon - c*T) appears when thermal expansion creates a stress-free strain shift
- Separable temperature and strain dependence → product form f(epsilon)*g(T) when mechanisms are independent
- Homologous temperature scaling → T often appears as (T - c0) or (c0 - T)/(c0 - c1) representing distance from a reference or melting temperature
- Concave-up stress-strain at large strains → polynomial with positive higher-order terms or exponential hardening exp(c*epsilon)
